## Section 001: Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names a polyglot theme without stating its organizing move, that idioms must stay classified by stack and layer, TypeScript branded types, Java records, Go error wrapping, Kafka idempotent producers, Terraform typed variables, instead of being flattened into language-neutral advice
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because all four mapped corpora organize by stack and layer, Idiom96 splits its library into TypeScript, Java, Go, DevOps, and Kafka parts, Idiom98 keeps per-stack sections with per-stack quality checklists, and broad-idiomatic-patterns mandates an L1 core, L2 std, L3 ecosystem split for Rust
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: layer-tagged guidance collapses when a task spans stacks at their integration seam, a Go service publishing Avro events to a Java consumer needs cross-stack contract idioms that no single language section carries
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference governs how to select and cite idiomatic patterns across the four mapped polyglot corpora, not how to teach any single language from scratch
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the stack-and-layer classification rule and name the five stacks the local corpus actually covers so readers route to the right pattern family immediately
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that layer classification is what makes idioms portable, the same accept-interfaces-return-structs shape appears as Go small interfaces, Java repository interfaces with constructor injection, and TypeScript IDatabase constructor parameters, so the layer label reveals the shared principle beneath the syntax
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to route any polyglot idiom question first to the matching stack section of Idiom96 or Idiom98, then check whether the idiom is a language-core, standard-library, or ecosystem-layer concern before adopting it
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because all four mapped corpora organize by stack and layer, Idiom96 splits its library into TypeScript, Java, Go, DevOps, and Kafka parts, Idiom98 keeps per-stack sections with per-stack quality checklists, and broad-idiomatic-patterns mandates an L1 core, L2 std, L3 ecosystem split for Rust
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; layer-tagged guidance collapses when a task spans stacks at their integration seam, a Go service publishing Avro events to a Java consumer needs cross-stack contract idioms that no single language section carries
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference governs how to select and cite idiomatic patterns across the four mapped polyglot corpora, not how to teach any single language from scratch
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open with the stack-and-layer classification rule and name the five stacks the local corpus actually covers so readers route to the right pattern family immediately
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Polyglot Idiomatic Reference Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies layer classification is what makes idioms portable, the same accept-interfaces-return-structs shape appears as Go small interfaces, Java repository interfaces with constructor injection, and TypeScript IDatabase constructor parameters, so the layer label reveals the shared principle beneath the syntax

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed map labels all four local rows with one generic role, historical idiomatic pattern corpus, hiding that they are four different instrument types, a pattern library, a TDD-workflow handbook, an extraction prompt, and a mined-codebase pattern report
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom96 is a flat catalog of stack idioms, Idiom98 wraps idioms in a stub-red-green-refactor delivery workflow with quality gates, broad-idiomatic-patterns is a prompt template for extracting new patterns, and opencode-genius documents patterns mined from one shipped TypeScript product
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the three external URL rows, the Codex AGENTS.md guide, GitHub Actions docs, and agents.md, were never retrieved in this evolution and cannot corroborate any polyglot idiom claim
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table records provenance for this document's claims and does not certify the external URLs as current or relevant
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to annotate each local row with its instrument type, catalog, workflow handbook, extraction prompt, or mined-pattern report, and mark all three external rows unretrieved
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the four instrument types compose into a pipeline, extract patterns with the broad prompt schema, catalog them Idiom96-style, operationalize them through Idiom98's TDD workflow, and validate them against a real codebase the way opencode-genius does

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement

- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom98 opens with the stub-red-green-refactor lifecycle, demonstrates it with parallel TypeScript, Java, and Go order-service implementations, and closes every stack with a checklist the tests and compilers can enforce

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide says start with the local map but not how an agent should choose between the two overlapping catalogs or when to consult the workflow file versus the pattern files
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus divides cleanly by question type, how-to-implement questions match Idiom96/Idiom98 stack sections, how-to-deliver questions match Idiom98's S01 workflow, how-to-extract questions match broad-idiomatic-patterns, and does-this-work-in-production questions match opencode-genius
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an agent following the guide literally could load 12,917 lines of corpus for a one-line idiom question, retrieval must be section-targeted, not file-targeted
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide steers agents choosing patterns within the mapped stacks, it does not authorize inventing idioms for unmapped languages
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a question-type routing list, implement, deliver, extract, validate, each pointing to its file and section family, plus an instruction to quote section identifiers in outputs

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scenario describes a generic uncertain user instead of the concrete journey the corpus serves, a developer landing in an unfamiliar stack of a polyglot codebase who must produce idiomatic code without months of immersion
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom98's naming conventions section is explicitly LLM-optimized and its parallel three-language order example exists precisely so one behavior can be compared across stacks by someone fluent in only one
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the journey breaks for a user whose target stack is absent, a Python or Rust-implementation task gets no catalog support here beyond the extraction prompt
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the journey covers cross-stack onboarding and review within the mapped stacks, not deep single-stack mastery
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recast the scenario as cross-stack translation, the user knows behavior X in their home stack and uses the parallel examples to express it idiomatically in the target stack
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the parallel order-service example is a Rosetta stone, mapping Result types to sealed interfaces to error returns teaches the translation function once, after which any pattern can be ported by analogy
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to have the newcomer read their home-stack version of a pattern first, then the target-stack version, then implement behind the target stack's gates
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Idiom98's naming conventions section is explicitly LLM-optimized and its parallel three-language order example exists precisely so one behavior can be compared across stacks by someone fluent in only one
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the journey breaks for a user whose target stack is absent, a Python or Rust-implementation task gets no catalog support here beyond the extraction prompt

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide frames adopt, adapt, avoid abstractly without the corpus's concrete tension, catalog fidelity versus target-codebase consistency when the surrounding repository already deviates from the catalogued idiom
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus itself encodes adaptations, Idiom98 presents both a hand-rolled Result namespace and the neverthrow library for the same need, and opencode-genius shows production code choosing bespoke solutions over textbook shapes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: adopting catalog idioms file-by-file inside a codebase with a different established convention produces two dialects, which the corpus's shotgun-surgery anti-pattern warns costs every future change
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide arbitrates pattern-level choices, repository-wide convention changes need a migration decision outside this reference
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a fourth column asking what the surrounding code already does, and rule that local consistency beats catalog fidelity until a deliberate migration is declared

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy

- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed hierarchy crowns Idiom96 canonical and demotes the other three to legacy, but Idiom98 is the deeper and more operational text, the only one with a delivery workflow, executable specifications, and per-stack quality gates
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because full reads show Idiom96 is a wide catalog while Idiom98 subsumes most of its stacks and adds the S01 TDD workflow, contract documentation, and 8,681 lines of worked patterns
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: canonical-versus-legacy is the wrong axis here, the four files rarely conflict, they occupy different roles, so demotion language suggests staleness that reading does not confirm
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the hierarchy governs precedence when the four mapped files disagree, it does not rank them for other themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to re-role the rows, Idiom98 canonical for workflow and depth, Idiom96 canonical for breadth and stacks Idiom98 lacks, opencode-genius supporting with production provenance, broad-idiomatic-patterns supporting as method
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that where the catalogs do overlap, Idiom98's variant is consistently the more defensive one, retry gains jitter and predicates, tests gain mock scaffolding, producers gain delivery timeouts, so overlap resolution can default to Idiom98
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to resolve any conflict between the two catalogs toward Idiom98's variant unless the task specifically needs Idiom96's wider stack coverage
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because full reads show Idiom96 is a wide catalog while Idiom98 subsumes most of its stacks and adds the S01 TDD workflow, contract documentation, and 8,681 lines of worked patterns

## Section 014: Worked Example Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed examples speak generically about loading sources while the corpus contains a ready-made worked spine, the order-creation service specified in Gherkin and implemented in TypeScript, Java, and Go through the stub, red, green, and refactor phases
- **supporting_reason:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom98 walks that single behavior end to end, failing tests for success and insufficient-stock paths, a minimal GREEN implementation, then a REFACTOR adding validation, correlation IDs, compensation, and structured logs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the order example is application-shaped, it exercises none of the Terraform, Kubernetes, or GitHub Actions idioms, so it cannot serve as the sole worked example for the infrastructure half of the corpus
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: worked examples here illustrate how to consume this reference, they are not tutorials replacing the corpus listings
- **revision_decision:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to anchor the good example on the order-service spine with its section citations, and add an infrastructure counterpart, the EKS module with typed, validated variables from section D.1.1
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the REFACTOR delta is the real lesson, comparing GREEN and refactored versions shows exactly which concerns, validation, compensation, observability, idiomatic code adds beyond passing tests
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds work at twelve source documents per use without reflecting this theme's real load shape, one enormous workflow file, one large catalog, and two small satellites totaling 12,917 lines that must never be loaded whole for a point question
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because full reads measured the imbalance, Idiom98 alone is 67 percent of the theme's lines, so retrieval cost is dominated by whether section targeting works, not by document count
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a document-count budget misprices the work, twelve small files are cheaper than one untargeted read of Idiom98

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed targets track label preservation and routing accuracy but omit the reliability property the corpus itself engineers for, that recommended idioms fail safe under partial failure, retries bounded, offsets committed after processing, reservations compensated
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom98's refactored order service compensates inventory reservations when persistence fails, its Kafka consumer acknowledges only after idempotency-checked processing, and both retry helpers cap attempts and delay
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: document-level reliability targets cannot certify runtime behavior, this section can only require that recommendations carry their fail-safe conditions, not that deployments honor them
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: targets here measure the reference's guidance quality, runtime SLOs belong to the consuming systems
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a target that 100 percent of failure-path recommendations name their bounded behavior, max attempts, compensation step, or acknowledgment condition, verifiable by reading the guidance
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the corpus treats reliability as a property of idiom choice, an idempotent producer plus manual commit makes at-least-once delivery safe by construction, so guidance completeness is a genuine upstream reliability control

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table lists document-drift failures but not the dominant failure of polyglot references, cross-stack blending, where an idiom valid in one stack is transplanted into another that has a different native shape
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus exists to prevent exactly that, it shows Optional is a return-type idiom in Java but an anti-pattern for parameters, and that panic is unacceptable for recoverable Go errors while exceptions are normal in Java
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: blending is hard to detect in review because transplanted code often compiles and passes shallow tests, only stack-native reviewers or lint rules catch the accent
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table catalogs failures of using this reference, not general production incident taxonomy
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add rows for cross-stack blending, GREEN-phase code quoted as final, unretrieved-URL laundering, and catalog-variant mixing, each with its trigger and mitigation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that all four added failures share one mechanism, provenance loss, the guidance detached from its stack, phase, retrieval status, or file of origin, so the single mitigation family is mandatory citation
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to when any output from this reference looks plausible but uncited, treat it as a suspected blend and re-derive it from a named section
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the corpus exists to prevent exactly that, it shows Optional is a return-type idiom in Java but an anti-pattern for parameters, and that panic is unacceptable for recoverable Go errors while exceptions are normal in Java
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; blending is hard to detect in review because transplanted code often compiles and passes shallow tests, only stack-native reviewers or lint rules catch the accent

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guidance covers retrying failed verification of this document but not the retry discipline the corpus prescribes for code, exponential backoff with jitter, retry predicates on error class, bounded attempts, and dead-letter escalation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom98's withRetry adds jitter and a shouldRetry predicate keyed to network errors and 5xx codes, its Kafka error handler pairs FixedBackOff of three attempts with a dead-letter recoverer, and its AsyncQueue bounds concurrency with timeouts
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: retry guidance for documents and for code must not merge, one bounded retry for stale evidence is a research policy, three broker redeliveries is a runtime policy, conflating them confuses both
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section governs both loops explicitly, document-verification retries and the code retry idioms this reference recommends, kept in separate paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the seed's document-loop rules and add the code-loop contract, classify the error, retry only transient classes, back off exponentially with jitter, cap attempts, then escalate to dead-letter or human
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure and idempotence are dual requirements, the corpus caps in-flight requests at five only because idempotence is enabled, retries without idempotent effects convert transient failures into duplicates
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to recommend retries only alongside their idempotence story, an idempotency key, an idempotent producer, or a naturally idempotent operation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Idiom98's withRetry adds jitter and a shouldRetry predicate keyed to network errors and 5xx codes, its Kafka error handler pairs FixedBackOff of three attempts with a dead-letter recoverer, and its AsyncQueue bounds concurrency with timeouts
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; retry guidance for documents and for code must not merge, one bounded retry for stale evidence is a research policy, three broker redeliveries is a runtime policy, conflating them confuses both

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checklist records document-usage evidence but omits the observability contract the corpus attaches to every service idiom, structured JSON logs with correlation IDs, RED metrics, health and readiness probes, and distributed tracing
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom98's observability checklist names each of those, its refactored order service threads a correlationId through every log line, and its Kubernetes manifests wire liveness and readiness probes with resource limits
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: observability advice divorced from the stack becomes boilerplate, probe endpoints matter in Kubernetes deployments, consumer lag matters for Kafka, reviewer-time metrics matter for documents, the checklist must say which applies where
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section keeps two ledgers, evidence about uses of this reference, and the code-observability items this reference tells builders to install
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain the document ledger and add the code ledger, correlation-ID logging, RED metrics, probes, tracing, and consumer-lag monitors, each tagged with its applicable stack
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that correlation IDs are the polyglot glue, the same request ID crossing a TypeScript gateway, a Java service, and a Kafka topic is what makes multi-stack failures diagnosable at all, which is why the corpus threads it through the REFACTOR phase rather than leaving it to operations
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to require every service recommendation from this reference to name its log structure, its metrics trio, and its probe or lag signal before it ships
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Idiom98's observability checklist names each of those, its refactored order service threads a correlationId through every log line, and its Kubernetes manifests wire liveness and readiness probes with resource limits

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed method measures reviewer navigation time but not the performance discipline the corpus builds into its idioms, P50/P99 latency requirements with critical-path tests, N+1 query avoidance, connection pooling, caching, and pagination
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Idiom98's performance checklist demands defined P50 and P99 targets with tests on critical paths, its JPA section exists largely to kill N+1 queries with fetch joins, and its Kafka producer config tunes batching, linger, and compression for throughput
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: document navigation speed and code latency are different quantities, a ten-minute review target says nothing about a 300ms P99, the method must keep the two measurements apart
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section verifies performance claims made by guidance from this reference, actual load testing belongs to the consuming project
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the reviewer-time gate for the document and add the code gate, any performance-relevant recommendation must name its target percentile, its measurement point, and the corpus idiom that serves it
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that most corpus performance idioms are structural rather than tuning, pooling, pagination, fetch joins, and async processing move complexity classes, so verifying their presence is cheaper and more durable than benchmarking constants

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement bounds document scale but not the scale seams the corpus marks in code, worker pools sized by explicit counts, queues with declared concurrency and timeouts, partition-keyed Kafka topics, and autoscaling bounded by HPA min and max
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every concurrency idiom in the corpus carries an explicit bound, the Go worker pool takes numWorkers, the AsyncQueue takes a concurrency option, the EKS node groups declare min, max, and desired sizes with at least two subnets for availability
